6,000\xc2\xa0kg (13,000\xc2\xa0lb), which can be all pressurized, all unpressurized or anywhere between. It can return to Earth 3,500\xc2\xa0kg (7,700\xc2\xa0lb), which can be all unpressurized disposal mass or up to 3,000\xc2\xa0kg (6,600\xc2\xa0lb) of return pressurized cargo\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dragon_6-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-Dragon-6">\n           [6]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th       </th>\n        <td>\n         1 week to 2 years\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sx20090918_5-3">\n          <a href="#cite_note-sx20090918-5">\n           [5]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row" style="padding-top:0.25em;line-height:1.25em;">\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Re-entry" title="Re-entry">\n Propellant\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Dinitrogen_tetroxide" title="Dinitrogen tetroxide">\n          NTO\n         </a>\n         /\n         <a href="/wiki/Monomethylhydrazine" title="Monomethylhydrazine">\n          MMH\n         </a>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FAA2012_9-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-FAA2012-9">\n           [9]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Dragon\n       </b>\n       is a reusable\n       <a href="/wiki/Spacecraft" title="Spacecraft">\n        spacecraft\n       </a>\n       developed by\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">\n        SpaceX\n       </a>\n       , an American\n       <a href="/wiki/Private_spaceflight" title="Private spaceflight">\n        private space\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_transport" title="Space transport">\n        transportation\n       </a>\n       company based in\n       <a href="/wiki/Hawthorne,_California" title="Hawthorne, California">\n        Hawthorne, California\n       </a>\n       . Dragon is launched into space by the SpaceX\n       <a href="/wiki/Falcon_9" title="Falcon 9">\n        Falcon 9\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Two-stage-to-orbit" title="Two-stage-to-orbit">\n        two-stage-to-orbit\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Launch_vehicle" title="Launch vehicle">\n        launch vehicle\n       </a>\n       , and SpaceX is developing a crewed version called the\n       <a href="/wiki/Dragon_2" title="Dragon 2">\n        Dragon V2\n       </a>\n       (formerly DragonRider). The Dragon spacecraft was originally designed for human travel, but so far has only been used to deliver cargo to the International Space Station (ISS). While carrying out resupply missions to the ISS, Space X has continued to work on the production of a human rated model. This model will be able to be controlled by the command center in Hawthorne, CA as well as by the crew of the spacecraft.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During its maiden flight in December 2010, Dragon became the first commercially built and operated spacecraft to be recovered successfully from orbit.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FirstFlight2010_2-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FirstFlight2010-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On 25 May 2012, a cargo variant of Dragon\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/COTS_Demo_Flight_2" title="COTS Demo Flight 2">\n        became the first commercial spacecraft\n       </a>\n       to successfully\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_rendezvous" title="Space rendezvous">\n        rendezvous\n       </a>\n       with and attach to the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       (ISS).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FirstDock_10-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FirstDock-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20120525_11-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20120525-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       SpaceX is contracted to deliver cargo to the ISS under\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n        NASA\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Resupply_Services" title="Commercial Resupply Services">\n        Commercial Resupply Services\n       </a>\n       program, and Dragon began regular cargo flights in October 2012.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InOrbitOctober2012_13-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-InOrbitOctober2012-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oct8Launch_14-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-oct8Launch-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sepLaunch_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sepLaunch-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-augLaunch_16-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-augLaunch-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       With the Dragon spacecraft and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Orbital_ATK" title="Orbital ATK">\n        Orbital ATK\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Cygnus_(spacecraft)" title="Cygnus (spacecraft)">\n        Cygnus\n       </a>\n       , NASA seeks to increase its partnerships with domestic commercial aviation and aeronautics industry.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-space-081223_17-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-space-081223-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 3 June 2017, the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CRS-11" title="CRS-11">\n        CRS-11\n       </a>\n       capsule largely assembled from previously flown components from the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CRS-4" title="CRS-4">\n        CRS-4\n       </a>\n       mission in September 2014 was launched again for the first time, with the hull, structural elements, thrusters, harnesses, propellant tanks, plumbing and many of the avionics reused while the heat shield, batteries and components exposed to sea water upon splashdown for recovery were replaced.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1">\n         <a href="#Name">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           1\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Name\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2">\n         <a href="#History">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           2\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           History\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3">\n           <a href="#NASA_ISS_resupply_contract">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             NASA ISS resupply contract\n            </span>\n           </a>\n           <ul>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-4">\n             <a Resupply Services Phase 1\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-6">\n             <a Resupply Services Phase 2\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-7">\n             <a href="#Demonstration_flights">\n </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-8">\n             <a href="#Operational_flights">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               2.1.5\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Operational flights\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n           </ul>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 development program\n            </span>\n           </a>\n           <ul>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-10">\n             <a href="#NASA_Commercial_Crew_Development_program">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               2.2.1\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               NASA Commercial Crew Development program\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n           </ul>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11">\n         <a href="#Development_funding">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           3\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Development funding\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12">\n         <a href="#Production">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           4\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Production\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13">\n         <a href="#Variants_and_Derivatives">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           5\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Variants and Derivatives\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14">\n           <a href="#Dragon_CRS">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Dragon CRS\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15">\n           <a href="#DragonLab">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             DragonLab\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16">\n           <a href="#Dragon_2">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Dragon 2\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17">\n           <a href="#Red_Dragon">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Red Dragon\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18">\n         <a href="#List_of_Dragon_missions">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           6\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           List of Dragon missions\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19">\n         <a href="#Specifications">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Specifications\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20">\n           <a href="#DragonLab_2">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             DragonLab\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21">\n           <a href="#Radiation_tolerance">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Radiation tolerance\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           9\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           10\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Name">\n        Name\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=SpaceX_Dragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       SpaceX\'s CEO,\n       <a href="/wiki/Elon_Musk" title="Elon Musk">\n        Elon Musk\n       </a>\n       , named the spacecraft after the 1963 song "\n       <a href="/wiki/Puff,_the_Magic_Dragon" title="Puff, the Magic Dragon">\n        Puff, the Magic Dragon\n       </a>\n       " by\n       <a href="/wiki/Peter,_Paul_and_Mary" title="Peter, Paul and Mary">\n        Peter, Paul and Mary\n       </a>\n       , reportedly as a response to critics who considered his spaceflight projects impossible.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=SpaceX_Dragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       SpaceX began\n       <a href="/wiki/New_product_development" title="New product development">\n        developing\n       </a>\n       the Dragon spacecraft in late 2004, making a public announcement in 2006 with a plan of entering service in 2009.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brian_20-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Brian-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Also in 2006, SpaceX won a contract to use the Dragon spacecraft for commercially supplied resupply services to the International Space Station for the American\n       <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">\n        federal\n       </a>\n       space agency, NASA.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfn20060818_21-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sfn20060818-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="NASA_ISS_resupply_contract">\n        NASA ISS resupply contract\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=SpaceX_Dragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: NASA ISS resupply contract">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_Orbital_Transportation_Services">\n        Commercial Orbital Transportation Services\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=SpaceX_Dragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Commercial Orbital Transportation Services">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       In 2005, NASA solicited proposals for a commercial ISS resupply cargo vehicle to replace the then-soon-to-be-retired\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_retirement" title="Space Shuttle retirement">\n        Space Shuttle\n       </a>\n       , through its\n       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Orbital_Transportation_Services" title="Commercial Orbital Transportation Services">\n        Commercial Orbital Transportation Services\n       </a>\n       (COTS) development program. The Dragon spacecraft was a part of SpaceX\'s proposal, submitted to NASA in March 2006. SpaceX\'s COTS proposal was issued as part of a team, which also included\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MD_Robotics" title="MD Robotics">\n        MD Robotics\n       </a>\n       , the Canadian company that had built the ISS\'s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadarm2" title="Canadarm2">\n        Canadarm2\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SpaceX_factory_Dragon_capsule.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3478" data-file-width="2725" height="217" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/SpaceX_factory_Dragon_capsule.jpg/170px-SpaceX_factory_Dragon_capsule.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/SpaceX_factory_Dragon_capsule.jpg/255px-SpaceX_factory_Dragon_capsule.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/SpaceX_factory_Dragon_capsule.jpg/340px-SpaceX_factory_Dragon_capsule.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SpaceX_factory_Dragon_capsule.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         An early Dragon pressure vessel, photographed during factory tests in 2008\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DragonEye_on_STS-133.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="357" data-file-width="456" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/DragonEye_on_STS-133.jpg/220px-DragonEye_on_STS-133.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/DragonEye_on_STS-133.jpg/330px-DragonEye_on_STS-133.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/DragonEye_on_STS-133.jpg/440px-DragonEye_on_STS-133.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DragonEye_on_STS-133.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The DragonEye system on\n         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Discovery" title="Space Shuttle Discovery">\n          Space Shuttle\n          <i>\n           Discovery\n          </i>\n         </a>\n         during\n         <a href="/wiki/STS-133" title="STS-133">\n          STS-133\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       On 18 August 2006, NASA announced that SpaceX had been chosen, along with\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kistler_Aerospace" title="Kistler Aerospace">\n        Kistler Aerospace\n       </a>\n       , to develop cargo launch services for the ISS.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfn20060818_21-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sfn20060818-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The initial plan called for three demonstration flights of SpaceX\'s Dragon spacecraft to be conducted between 2008 and 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msnbc_COTS_contract_20080818_23-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-msnbc_COTS_contract_20080818-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       SpaceX and Kistler were to receive up to $278 million and $207 million respectively,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msnbc_COTS_contract_20080818_23-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-msnbc_COTS_contract_20080818-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       if they met all NASA milestones, but Kistler failed to meet its obligations, and its contract was terminated in 2007.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RpK_Plug_Pulled_24-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-RpK_Plug_Pulled-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       NASA later re-awarded Kistler\'s contract to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orbital_Sciences" title="Orbital Sciences">\n        Orbital Sciences\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RpK_Plug_Pulled_24-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-RpK_Plug_Pulled-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NSF-COTS_25-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NSF-COTS-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_Resupply_Services_Phase_1">\n        Commercial Resupply Services Phase 1\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=SpaceX_Dragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Commercial Resupply Services Phase 1">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       On 23 December 2008, NASA awarded a $1.6 billion\n       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Resupply_Services" title="Commercial Resupply Services">\n        Commercial Resupply Services\n       </a>\n       (CRS) contract to SpaceX, with contract options that could potentially increase the maximum contract value to $3.1 billion.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SpaceX_Cargo_Contract_20081223_26-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SpaceX_Cargo_Contract_20081223-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The contract called for 12 flights to the ISS, with a minimum of 20,000\xc2\xa0kg (44,000\xc2\xa0lb) of cargo carried to the ISS.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SpaceX_Cargo_Contract_20081223_26-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SpaceX_Cargo_Contract_20081223-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 23 February 2009, SpaceX announced that its chosen phenolic-impregnated carbon ablator heat shield material, PICA-X, had passed heat stress tests in preparation for Dragon\'s maiden launch.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n        <a href="#cite_note-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-a.26s201201_28-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-a.26s201201-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The primary proximity-operations sensor for the Dragon spacecraft, the DragonEye, was tested in early 2009 during the\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-127" title="STS-127">\n        STS-127\n       </a>\n       mission, when it was mounted near the docking port of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Endeavour" title="Space Shuttle Endeavour">\n        Space Shuttle\n        <i>\n         Endeavour\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       and used while the Shuttle approached the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       . The DragonEye\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Lidar" title="Lidar">\n        Lidar\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Thermography" title="Thermography">\n        thermography\n       </a>\n       (thermal imaging) abilities were both tested successfully.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SpaceX_Update_20090923_29-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SpaceX_Update_20090923-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The COTS UHF Communication Unit (CUCU) and Crew Command Panel (CCP) were delivered to the ISS during the late 2009\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-129" title="STS-129">\n        STS-129\n       </a>\n       mission.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CUCU_31-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CUCU-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The CUCU allows the ISS to communicate with Dragon and the CCP allows ISS crew members to issue basic commands to Dragon.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CUCU_31-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CUCU-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In summer 2009, SpaceX hired former\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n        NASA\n       </a>\n       astronaut\n       <a href="/wiki/Ken_Bowersox" title="Ken Bowersox">\n        Ken Bowersox\n       </a>\n       as vice president of their new Astronaut Safety and Mission Assurance Department, in preparation for crews using the spacecraft.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As a condition of the NASA CRS contract, SpaceX analyzed the orbital\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_radiation" title="Space radiation">\n        radiation environment\n       </a>\n       on all Dragon systems, and how the spacecraft would respond to spurious radiation events. That analysis and the Dragon design \xe2\x80\x93 which uses an overall\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fault-tolerant" title="Fault-tolerant">\n        fault-tolerant\n       </a>\n       triple-redundant computer architecture, rather than individual\n       <a href="/wiki/Radiation_hardening" title="Radiation hardening">\n        radiation hardening\n       </a>\n       of each computer processor \xe2\x80\x93 was reviewed by independent experts before being approved by NASA for the cargo flights.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aw20121118_33-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-aw20121118-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During March, 2015, it was announced that SpaceX had been awarded an additional three missions under Commercial Resupply Services Phase 1.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nsf-20150303nasacrs1addlaward_34-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nsf-20150303nasacrs1addlaward-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       These additional missions are\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-13" title="SpaceX CRS-13">\n        SpaceX CRS-13\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-14" title="SpaceX CRS-14">\n        SpaceX CRS-14\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-15" title="SpaceX CRS-15">\n        SpaceX CRS-15\n       </a>\n       and would cover the cargo needs of 2017.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 24 February 2016, SpaceNews disclosed that SpaceX had been awarded a further five missions under Commercial Resupply Services Phase 1.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sn-20160224spxwinsaddlcrs1_35-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sn-20160224spxwinsaddlcrs1-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This additional tranche of missions had\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-16" title="SpaceX CRS-16">\n        SpaceX CRS-16\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-17" title="SpaceX CRS-17">\n        SpaceX CRS-17\n       </a>\n       manifested for FY2017 while\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-18" title="SpaceX CRS-18">\n        SpaceX CRS-18\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-19" title="SpaceX CRS-19">\n        SpaceX CRS-19\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-20" title="SpaceX CRS-20">\n        SpaceX CRS-20\n       </a>\n       and were notionally manifested for FY2018.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_Resupply_Services_Phase_2">\n        Commercial Resupply Services Phase 2\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=SpaceX_Dragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Commercial Resupply Services Phase 2">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <i>\n        Commercial Resupply Services 2\n       </i>\n       (CRS2) contract definition/solicitation period commenced in 2014 and a result announced on 14 January 2016. The CRS2 launches are expected to commence in 2019, and extend to at least 2024. On 14 January 2016, NASA announced that three companies had been awarded contracts for a minimum of six launches each.\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">\n        SpaceX\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Orbital_ATK" title="Orbital ATK">\n        Orbital ATK\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Nevada_Corporation" title="Sierra Nevada Corporation">\n        Sierra Nevada Corporation\n       </a>\n       won contracts.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WashintonPostJan142016_36-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WashintonPostJan142016-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The maximum potential value of all the contracts was indicated to be $14Bn but the minimum requirements would be considerably less. No further financial information was disclosed. The missions involved would be from late 2019 through to 2024.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demonstration_flights">\n        Demonstration flights\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=SpaceX_Dragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Demonstration flights">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:COTS2_Dragon_is_berthed.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2832" data-file-width="3402" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/COTS2_Dragon_is_berthed.jpg/220px-COTS2_Dragon_is_berthed.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/COTS2_Dragon_is_berthed.jpg/330px-COTS2_Dragon_is_berthed.jpg 1.5x, the\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadarm2" title="Canadarm2">\n          Canadarm2\n         </a>\n         manipulator during the COTS 2 mission\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Inside_the_Dragon_(capsule).jpg">\n         <img alt=""        <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Inside_the_Dragon_(capsule).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Interior of the COTS 2 Dragon capsule.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image"
