      <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Space_X_water3.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Recovery of the COTS 2 Dragon capsule on 31 May 2012.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:315px;max-width:315px">\n        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:175px;max-width:175px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SpX_CRS-2_launch_-_cropped.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="1996" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/SpX_CRS-2_launch_-_cropped.jpg/173px-SpX_CRS-2_launch_-_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/SpX_CRS-2_launch_-_cropped.jpg/260px-SpX_CRS-2_launch_-_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/SpX_CRS-2_launch_-_cropped.jpg/346px-SpX_CRS-2_launch_-_cropped.jpg 2x" width="173"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          The Dragon spacecraft being launched on a\n          <a href="/wiki/Falcon_9_v1.0" title="Falcon 9 v1.0">\n           Falcon 9 v1.0\n          </a>\n          rocket\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:136px;max-width:136px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SpX-3_launch.1.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="1647" data-file-width="1311" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/SpX-3_launch.1.jpg/134px-SpX-3_launch.1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/SpX-3_launch.1.jpg/201px-SpX-3_launch.1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/SpX-3_launch.1.jpg/268px-SpX-3_launch.1.jpg 2x" width="134"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          The Dragon spacecraft being launched on a\n          <a href="/wiki/Falcon_9_v1.1" title="Falcon 9 v1.1">\n           Falcon 9 v1.1\n          </a>\n          rocket\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div style="clear:left">\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The first flight of the Falcon 9, a\n       <a href="/wiki/Private_spaceflight" title="Private spaceflight">\n        private\n       </a>\n       flight, occurred in June 2010 and launched a\n       <a href="/wiki/Boilerplate_(spaceflight)" title="Boilerplate (spaceflight)">\n        stripped-down\n       </a>\n       version of the Dragon capsule. This\n       <a href="/wiki/Dragon_Spacecraft_Qualification_Unit" title="Dragon Spacecraft Qualification Unit">\n        Dragon Spacecraft Qualification Unit\n       </a>\n       had initially been used as a ground test bed to validate several of the capsule\'s systems. During the flight, the unit\'s primary mission was to relay aerodynamic data captured during the ascent.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It was not designed to survive re-entry, and did not.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       NASA contracted for three test flights from SpaceX, but later reduced that number to two. The first Dragon spacecraft launched on its first mission \xe2\x80\x93 contracted to NASA as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/COTS_Demo_Flight_1" title="COTS Demo Flight 1">\n        COTS Demo Flight 1\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x93 on 8 December 2010, and was successfully recovered following re-entry to Earth\'s atmosphere. The mission also marked the second flight of the Falcon 9 launch vehicle.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCLaunchDec2010_40-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BBCLaunchDec2010-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The DragonEye sensor flew again on\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-133" title="STS-133">\n        STS-133\n       </a>\n       in February 2011 for further on-orbit testing.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In November 2010, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">\n        Federal Aviation Administration\n       </a>\n       (FAA) had issued a re-entry license for the Dragon capsule, the first such license ever awarded to a commercial vehicle.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/COTS_Demo_Flight_2" title="COTS Demo Flight 2">\n        second Dragon flight\n       </a>\n       , also contracted to NASA as a demonstration mission, launched successfully on 22 May 2012, after NASA had approved SpaceX\'s proposal to combine the COTS 2 and 3 mission objectives into a single Falcon 9/Dragon flight, renamed COTS 2+.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LaunchAtLast_3-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LaunchAtLast-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spaceflight_Now_20111209_43-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Spaceflight_Now_20111209-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Dragon conducted orbital tests of its navigation systems and abort procedures, before being grappled by the ISS\'\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadarm2" title="Canadarm2">\n        Canadarm2\n       </a>\n       and successfully berthing with the station on 25 May to offload its cargo.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FirstDock_10-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FirstDock-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WiredBerth_44-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WiredBerth-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">\n        <a href="#cite_note-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Dragon returned to Earth on 31 May 2012, landing as scheduled in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">\n        Pacific Ocean\n       </a>\n       , and was again successfully recovered.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Accomplished_48-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Accomplished-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n        <a href="#cite_note-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 23 August 2012, NASA Administrator\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Bolden" title="Charles Bolden">\n        Charles Bolden\n       </a>\n       announced that SpaceX had completed all required milestones under the COTS contract, and was cleared to begin\n       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Resupply_Services" title="Commercial Resupply Services">\n        operational resupply missions to the ISS\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Operational_flights">\n        Operational flights\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=SpaceX_Dragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Operational flights">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       From October 2012 to August 2017, Dragon successfully completed 11 of 12 attempted resupply missions to the International Space Station.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Dragon was launched on its\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-1" title="SpaceX CRS-1">\n        first operational CRS-contract mission\n       </a>\n       on 8 October 2012,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InOrbitOctober2012_13-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-InOrbitOctober2012-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and completed the mission successfully on 28 October.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc20121028_51-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bbc20121028-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-2" title="SpaceX CRS-2">\n        SpaceX CRS-2\n       </a>\n       , the second CRS mission from SpaceX, was successfully launched on 1 March 2013.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-3" title="SpaceX CRS-3">\n        SpaceX CRS-3\n       </a>\n       , SpaceX\'s third CRS mission, was launched on 18 April 2014 and was berthed with the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISS" title="ISS">\n        ISS\n       </a>\n       from 20 April 2014 through 18 May 2014.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-4" title="SpaceX CRS-4">\n        SpaceX CRS-4\n       </a>\n       successfully launched on Sunday, 21 September 2014 and berthed with the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISS" title="ISS">\n        ISS\n       </a>\n       on Tuesday, 23 September. It splashed down in the Pacific Ocean carrying 3,276 pounds of cargo and science samples.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n        <a href="#cite_note-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-5" title="SpaceX CRS-5">\n        SpaceX CRS-5\n       </a>\n       , SpaceX\'s fifth CRS mission, was scheduled for launch on December 9, 2014, but was delayed over several dates in December. The launch was rescheduled to Saturday, January 10, 2015, which completed successfully at 4:47 AM Central time.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CRS-5_54-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CRS-5-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-6" title="SpaceX CRS-6">\n        SpaceX CRS-6\n       </a>\n       , SpaceX\'s sixth CRS mission, was successfully launched on April 14, 2015, at 20:10:41 UTC from\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Canaveral_Air_Force_Station" title="Cape Canaveral Air Force Station">\n        Cape Canaveral Air Force Station\n       </a>\n       in Florida.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-7" title="SpaceX CRS-7">\n        SpaceX CRS-7\n       </a>\n       , SpaceX\'s seventh CRS mission, was attempted on June 28, 2015 from\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Canaveral_Air_Force_Station" title="Cape Canaveral Air Force Station">\n        Cape Canaveral Air Force Station\n       </a>\n       in Florida. The mission was unsuccessful, with an anomaly occurring during the ascent of the first stage, resulting in an explosion and a total loss of the vehicle.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-8" title="SpaceX CRS-8">\n        SpaceX CRS-8\n       </a>\n       , SpaceX\'s eighth CRS mission, was successfully launched on April 8, 2016 from\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Canaveral_Air_Force_Station" title="Cape Canaveral Air Force Station">\n        Cape Canaveral Air Force Station\n       </a>\n       in Florida. The first stage landed successfully on SpaceX\'s drone ship in the Atlantic Ocean, and was subsequently reused to launch\n       <a href="/wiki/SES-10" title="SES-10">\n        SES-10\n       </a>\n       on March 30, 2017.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-9" title="SpaceX CRS-9">\n        SpaceX CRS-9\n       </a>\n       , SpaceX\'s ninth CRS mission, was successfully launched on July 18, 2016 from\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Canaveral_Air_Force_Station" title="Cape Canaveral Air Force Station">\n        Cape Canaveral Air Force Station\n       </a>\n       in Florida. The first stage landed successfully at\n       <a href="/wiki/Landing_Zone_1" title="Landing Zone 1">\n        Landing Zone 1\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-10" title="SpaceX CRS-10">\n        SpaceX CRS-10\n       </a>\n       , SpaceX\'s tenth CRS mission, was aborted on February 18, 2017 due to an anomaly in the Thrust Vector Control (TVC) of the second stage but successfully launched on the February 19th from\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">\n        Kennedy Space Center\n       </a>\n       in Florida. The first stage landed successfully on\n       <a href="/wiki/Landing_Zone_1" title="Landing Zone 1">\n        Landing Zone 1\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-11" title="SpaceX CRS-11">\n        SpaceX CRS-11\n       </a>\n       , SpaceX\'s eleventh CRS mission, was successfully launched on June 3, 2017 from\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">\n        Kennedy Space Center\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LC-39A" title="LC-39A">\n        LC-39A\n       </a>\n       , being the 100th mission to be launched from that pad. This mission was the first to re-fly a recovered Dragon capsule that previously flew on\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-4" title="SpaceX CRS-4">\n        CRS-4\n       </a>\n       mission. This mission delivered 2,708 kilograms\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dragon_reused_55-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Dragon_reused-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       of cargo to the International Space Station, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Neutron_Star_Interior_Composition_Explorer" title="Neutron Star Interior Composition Explorer">\n        NICER\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa-nicer-manifest_56-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nasa-nicer-manifest-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The first stage of the Falcon 9 launch vehicle landed successfully at\n       <a href="/wiki/Landing_Zone_1" title="Landing Zone 1">\n        Landing Zone 1\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-12" title="SpaceX CRS-12">\n        SpaceX CRS-12\n       </a>\n       , SpaceX\'s twelfth CRS mission, was successfully launched on the first \'Block 4\' version of the Falcon 9 on August 14, 2017 from\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">\n        Kennedy Space Center\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LC-39A" title="LC-39A">\n        LC-39A\n       </a>\n       at the first attempt. This mission delivered 2,349 kg (5,179 lb) of pressurized mass and 961 kg (2,119 lb) unpressurized. The external payload manifested for this flight was the CREAM cosmic-ray detector. Last flight of a newly-built Dragon capsule; further missions will use refurbished spacecraft.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n        <a href="#cite_note-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Crewed_development_program">\n        Crewed development program\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=SpaceX_Dragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Crewed development program">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SpaceX_Dragon_v2_Pad_Abort_Vehicle_(16661791299).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/SpaceX_Dragon_v2_Pad_Abort_Vehicle_%2816661791299%29.jpg/220px-SpaceX_Dragon_v2_Pad_Abort_Vehicle_%2816661791299%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/SpaceX_Dragon_v2_Pad_Abort_Vehicle_%2816661791299%29.jpg/330px-SpaceX_Dragon_v2_Pad_Abort_Vehicle_%2816661791299%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/SpaceX_Dragon_v2_Pad_Abort_Vehicle_%2816661791299%29.jpg/440px-SpaceX_Dragon_v2_Pad_Abort_Vehicle_%2816661791299%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SpaceX_Dragon_v2_Pad_Abort_Vehicle_(16661791299).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Exterior of the Dragon 2 used for the\n         <a href="/wiki/Pad_abort_test" title="Pad abort test">\n          pad abort test\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dragon_V2_interior.2.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Dragon_V2_interior.2.jpg/220px-Dragon_V2_interior.2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Dragon_V2_interior.2.jpg/330px-Dragon_V2_interior.2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Dragon_V2_interior.2.jpg/440px-Dragon_V2_interior.2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dragon_V2_interior.2.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Interior of the Dragon 2 capsule, showing the seat configuration\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 2006, Elon Musk stated that SpaceX had built "a prototype flight crew capsule, including a thoroughly tested 30-man-day life-support system".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brian_20-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Brian-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A video simulation of this escape system\'s operation was released in January 2011.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sxvid20110114_58-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sxvid20110114-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Musk stated in 2010 that the developmental cost of a crewed Dragon and Falcon 9 would be between $800 million and $1 billion.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2009 and 2010, Musk suggested on several occasions that plans for a crewed variant of the Dragon were proceeding and had a two-to-three-year timeline to completion.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-This_Week_in_Space_60-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-This_Week_in_Space-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Augustine_61-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Augustine-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       SpaceX submitted a bid for the third phase of CCDev,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CCiCap" title="CCiCap">\n        CCiCap\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gov_63-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-gov-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="NASA_Commercial_Crew_Development_program">\n        NASA Commercial Crew Development program\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=SpaceX_Dragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: NASA Commercial Crew Development program">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       SpaceX was not awarded funding during the first phase of NASA\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Crew_Development" title="Commercial Crew Development">\n        Commercial Crew Development\n       </a>\n       (CCDev) milestone-based program. However, the company was selected on 18 April 2011, during the second phase of the program, to receive an award valued at $75 million to help develop its crew system.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n        <a href="#cite_note-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n        <a href="#cite_note-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Their CCDev2 milestones involved the further advancement of the Falcon 9/Dragon crew transportation design, the advancement of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Launch_escape_system" title="Launch escape system">\n        Launch Abort System\n       </a>\n       propulsion design, completion of two crew accommodations demos, full-duration test firings of the launch abort engines, and demonstrations of their throttle capability.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">\n        <a href="#cite_note-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       SpaceX\'s launch abort system received preliminary design approval from NASA in October 2011.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wired_Abort_Approved_20111027_67-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Wired_Abort_Approved_20111027-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In December 2011, SpaceX performed its first crew accommodations test; the second such test is expected to involve\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spacesuit" title="Spacesuit">\n        spacesuit\n       </a>\n       simulators and a higher-fidelity crewed Dragon mock-up.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n        <a href="#cite_note-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n        <a href="#cite_note-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In January 2012, SpaceX successfully conducted full-duration tests of its SuperDraco landing/escape rocket engine at its Rocket Development Facility in\n       <a href="/wiki/McGregor,_Texas" title="McGregor, Texas">\n        McGregor, Texas\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n        <a href="#cite_note-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dragon_Pad_Abort_Test.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2008" data-file-width="3000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Dragon_Pad_Abort_Test.jpg/220px-Dragon_Pad_Abort_Test.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Dragon_Pad_Abort_Test.jpg/330px-Dragon_Pad_Abort_Test.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Dragon_Pad_Abort_Test.jpg/440px-Dragon_Pad_Abort_Test.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dragon_Pad_Abort_Test.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Dragon during its\n         <a href="/wiki/Pad_abort_test" title="Pad abort test">\n          pad abort test\n         </a>\n         on 6 May 2015\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       On 3 August 2012, NASA announced the award of $440 million to SpaceX for the continuation of work on the Dragon under CCiCap.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">\n        <a href="#cite_note-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On 20 December 2013, SpaceX completed a parachute drop test to validate the new parachute design.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">\n        <a href="#cite_note-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This involved carrying a 5,400 kilograms (12,000\xc2\xa0lb) Dragon test article by helicopter to an altitude of 2,400 meters (8,000\xc2\xa0ft) above the Pacific Ocean.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASAPARA_73-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NASAPARA-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The test article was released and intentionally forced into a tumble.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASAPARA_73-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NASAPARA-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Dragon then released its two\n       <a href="/wiki/Drogue_parachute" title="Drogue parachute">\n        drogue parachutes\n       </a>\n       , followed by its three main parachutes and splashed down into the ocean.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASAPARA_73-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NASAPARA-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The test article was then retrieved by helicopter and returned to shore.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASAPARA_73-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NASAPARA-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 6 May 2015, SpaceX completed a pad abort test for the Dragon 2.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASApadabort_74-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NASApadabort-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFNPadAbort_75-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SFNPadAbort-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SNPadAbort_76-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SNPadAbort-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NSFPadAbort_77-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NSFPadAbort-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       During this test, the Dragon used its abort engines to launch away from a test stand at Launch Complex 40.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASApadabort_74-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NASApadabort-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFNPadAbort_75-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SFNPadAbort-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NSFPadAbort_77-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NSFPadAbort-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It traveled to an altitude of 1,187 meters (3,894\xc2\xa0ft),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">\n        <a href="#cite_note-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       separated from its trunk, deployed its drogue parachutes and then the main parachutes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFNPadAbort_75-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SFNPadAbort-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NSFPadAbort_77-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NSFPadAbort-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It splashed down into the ocean and was recovered.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFNPadAbort_75-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SFNPadAbort-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NSFPadAbort_77-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NSFPadAbort-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The vehicle was planned to reach an altitude of 1,500 meters (5,000\xc2\xa0ft) but one of the engines underperformed due to an abnormal fuel mixture ratio.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFNPadAbort_75-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SFNPadAbort-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SNPadAbort_76-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SNPadAbort-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Dragon flown is planned to be refurbished for the in-flight abort test.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SNPadAbort_76-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SNPadAbort-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NSFPadAbort_77-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NSFPadAbort-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In a planned in-flight abort test, Dragon will use its launch abort engines to escape from a modified Falcon 9 that is already in flight.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CCiCap20120724_79-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CCiCap20120724-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FloPadAbort_80-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FloPadAbort-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The launch is planned to occur from\n       <a href="/wiki/Vandenberg_AFB_Space_Launch_Complex_4#SLC-4E" title="Vandenberg AFB Space Launch Complex 4">\n        SLC-4E\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NSFPadAbort_77-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NSFPadAbort-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This test will occur at the point of worst-case dynamic loads, which is also when Dragon has the smallest performance margin for separation from its launch vehicle.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CCiCap20120724_79-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CCiCap20120724-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Falcon 9 planned to be used will only have three engines on the first stage and will have no second stage.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NSFPadAbort_77-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NSFPadAbort-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       An uncrewed test mission to the ISS,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SpX-DM1" title="SpX-DM1">\n        SpX-DM1\n       </a>\n       , is planned to be launched in November 2017.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">\n        <a href="#cite_note-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NSFinflightabort_82-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NSFinflightabort-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It will be a 30-day mission that will spend the majority of its time docked to the space station.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NSFinflightabort_82-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NSFinflightabort-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It will then land in the ocean and be retrieved.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NSFinflightabort_82-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NSFinflightabort-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A crewed test mission to the ISS,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SpX-DM2" title="SpX-DM2">\n        SpX-DM2\n       </a>\n       , is planned to be launched in May 2018 and last for 14 days.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shotwell-crewdragon_83-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-shotwell-crewdragon-83">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Development_funding">\n        Development funding\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=SpaceX_Dragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Development funding">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       In 2014, SpaceX released the total combined development costs for both the Falcon 9 launch vehicle and the Dragon capsule. NASA provided\n       <span style="white-space: nowrap">\n        US$396 million\n       </span>\n       while SpaceX provided over\n       <span style="white-space: nowrap">\n        US$450 million\n       </span>\n       to fund both development efforts.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AtlanticCouncil20140604_84-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AtlanticCouncil20140604-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Production">\n        Production\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=SpaceX_Dragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Production">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dragon_capsule_being_shipped_out_of_SpaceX_Hawthorne_facility_(16655995541).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Dragon_capsule_being_shipped_out_of_SpaceX_Hawthorne_facility_%2816655995541%29.jpg/220px-Dragon_capsule_being_shipped_out_of_SpaceX_Hawthorne_facility_%2816655995541%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Dragon_capsule_being_shipped_out_of_SpaceX_Hawthorne_facility_%2816655995541%29.jpg/330px-Dragon_capsule_being_shipped_out_of_SpaceX_Hawthorne_facility_%2816655995541%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Dragon_capsule_being_shipped_out_of_SpaceX_Hawthorne_facility_%2816655995541%29.jpg/440px-Dragon_capsule_being_shipped_out_of_SpaceX_Hawthorne_facility_%2816655995541%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dragon_capsule_being_shipped_out_of_SpaceX_Hawthorne_facility_(16655995541).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A Dragon capsule being shipped out of SpaceX HQ in Hawthorne, California, February 2015.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In December 2010, the SpaceX production line was reported to be manufacturing one new Dragon spacecraft and Falcon 9 rocket every three months. Elon Musk stated in a 2010 interview that he planned to increase production turnover to one Dragon every six weeks by 2012.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Space_Interview_20101209_85-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Space_Interview_20101209-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Composite_material" title="Composite material">\n        Composite materials\n       </a>\n       are extensively used in the spacecraft\'s manufacture to reduce weight and improve structural strength.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">\n        <a href="#cite_note-86">\n         [86]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       By September 2013, SpaceX total manufacturing space had increased to nearly 1,000,000 square feet (93,000\xc2\xa0m\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) and the factory had six Dragons in various stages of production. SpaceX published a photograph showing the six, including the next four NASA Commercial Resupply Services (CRS) mission Dragons (\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-3" title="SpaceX CRS-3">\n        CRS-3\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-4" title="SpaceX CRS-4">\n        CRS-4\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-5" title="SpaceX CRS-5">\n        CRS-5\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-6" title="SpaceX CRS-6">\n        CRS-6\n       </a>\n       ) plus the drop-test Dragon, and the pad-abort Dragon\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weldment" title="Weldment">\n        weldment\n       </a>\n       for commercial crew.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sxProd20130924_87-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sxProd20130924-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Variants_and_Derivatives">\n        Variants and Derivatives\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=SpaceX_Dragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Variants and Derivatives">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Dragon_CRS">\n        Dragon CRS\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=SpaceX_Dragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Dragon CRS">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dragon_spacecraft_press_and_unpress_sections.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="709" data-file-width="956" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Dragon_spacecraft_press_and_unpress_sections.png/220px-Dragon_spacecraft_press_and_unpress_sections.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Dragon_spacecraft_press_and_unpress_sections.png/330px-Dragon_spacecraft_press_and_unpress_sections.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Dragon_spacecraft_press_and_unpress_sections.png/440px-Dragon_spacecraft_press_and_unpress_sections.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dragon_spacecraft_press_and_unpress_sections.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Drawing showing the pressurized (red) and unpressurized (orange) sections of Dragon V1\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Dragon spacecraft consists of a nose-cone cap that jettisons after launch, a conventional blunt-cone\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_capsule" title="Space capsule">\n        ballistic capsule\n       </a>\n       , and an unpressurized cargo-carrier trunk equipped with two solar arrays.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-overview_88-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-overview-88">\n         [88]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The capsule uses a PICA-X heat shield, based on a proprietary variant of NASA\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_entry#Phenolic_impregnated_carbon_ablator" title="Atmospheric entry">\n        Phenolic impregnated carbon ablator\n       </a>\n       (PICA) material, designed to protect the capsule during Earth\n       <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_entry" title="Atmospheric entry">\n        atmospheric entry\n       </a>\n       , even at high return velocities from Lunar and Martian missions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2ndF9arrives_89-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2ndF9arrives-89">\n         [89]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sx-update20071210_90-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sx-update20071210-90">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">\n        <a href="#cite_note-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Dragon capsule is re-usable, and can fly multiple missions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-overview_88-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-overview-88">\n         [88]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The trunk is not recoverable; it separates from the capsule before re-entry and burns up in Earth\'s atmosphere.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">\n        <a href="#cite_note-92">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The trunk section, which carries the spacecraft\'s solar panels and allows the transport of unpressurized cargo to the ISS, was first used for cargo on the\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-2" title="SpaceX CRS-2">\n        SpaceX CRS-2\n       </a>\n       mission.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dragon_CRS-01.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2409" data-file-width="3416" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Dragon_CRS-01.jpg/220px-Dragon_CRS-01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Dragon_CRS-01.jpg/330px-Dragon_CRS-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Dragon_CRS-01.jpg/440px-Dragon_CRS-01.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dragon_CRS-01.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Dragon CRS 3 views\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dragon_CRS-02.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2436" data-file-width="3432" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Dragon_CRS-02.jpg/220px-Dragon_CRS-02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Dragon_CRS-02.jpg/330px-Dragon_CRS-02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Dragon_CRS-02.jpg/440px-Dragon_CRS-02.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dragon_CRS-02.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Dragon CRS 3 views\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dragon_CRS_Isometric.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2407" data-file-width="3423" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Dragon_CRS_Isometric.jpg/220px-Dragon_CRS_Isometric.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Dragon_CRS_Isometric.jpg/330px-Dragon_CRS_Isometric.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Dragon_CRS_Isometric.jpg/440px-Dragon_CRS_Isometric.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dragon_CRS_Isometric.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Dragon CRS\n         <a href="/wiki/Isometric_projection" title="Isometric projection">\n          Isometric view\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The spacecraft is launched atop a\n       <a href="/wiki/Falcon_9" title="Falcon 9">\n        Falcon 9\n       </a>\n       booster.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popmech-dec06-31_93-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-popmech-dec06-31-93">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Dragon capsule is equipped with 18\n       <a href="/wiki/Draco_(rocket_engine_family)" title="Draco (rocket engine family)">\n        Draco\n       </a>\n       thrusters.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sx-update20071210_90-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sx-update20071210-90">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       During its initial cargo and crew flights, the Dragon capsule will land in the Pacific Ocean and be returned to the shore by ship.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">\n        <a href="#cite_note-94">\n         [94]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       For the ISS Dragon cargo flights, the ISS\'s Canadarm2 grapples its\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flight-Releasable_Grapple_Fixture" title="Flight-Releasable Grapple Fixture">\n        Flight-Releasable Grapple Fixture\n       </a>\n       and berths Dragon to the station\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/US_Orbital_Segment" title="US Orbital Segment">\n        US Orbital Segment\n       </a>\n       using a\n       <a href="/wiki/Common_Berthing_Mechanism" title="Common Berthing Mechanism">\n        Common Berthing Mechanism\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">\n        <a href="#cite_note-95">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The CRS Dragon does not have an independent means of maintaining a breathable atmosphere for astronauts and instead circulates in fresh air from the ISS.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">\n        <a href="#cite_note-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For typical missions, Dragon is planned to remain berthed to the ISS for about 30 days.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">\n        <a href="#cite_note-97">\n         [97]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The CRS Dragon\'s capsule can transport 3,310\xc2\xa0kg (7,300\xc2\xa0lb) of cargo, which can be all pressurized, all unpressurized, or anywhere between. It can return to Earth 3,310\xc2\xa0kg (7,300\xc2\xa0lb), which can be all unpressurized disposal mass, or up to 2,500\xc2\xa0kg of return pressurized cargo, driven by parachute limitations. There is a volume constraint of 14\xc2\xa0m\n       <sup>\n        3\n       </sup>\n       (490\xc2\xa0cu\xc2\xa0ft) trunk unpressurized cargo and 11.2\xc2\xa0m\n       <sup>\n        3\n       </sup>\n       (400\xc2\xa0cu\xc2\xa0ft) of pressurized cargo (up or down).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISS-1_98-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ISS-1-98">\n         [98]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The trunk was first used operationally on the Dragon\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-2" title="SpaceX CRS-2">\n        CRS-2\n       </a>\n       mission in March 2013.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nsf20121019_99-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nsf20121019-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Its solar arrays produce a peak power of 4\xc2\xa0kW.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FAA2012_9-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FAA2012-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The CRS Dragon design was modified beginning with the fifth Dragon flight on the\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-3" title="SpaceX CRS-3">\n        SpaceX CRS-3\n       </a>\n       mission to the ISS in March 2014. While the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Outer_mold_line" title="Outer mold line">\n        outer mold line\n       </a>\n       of the Dragon was unchanged, the avionics and cargo racks were redesigned to supply substantially more\n       <a href="/wiki/Solar_panels_on_spacecraft" title="Solar panels on spacecraft">\n        electrical power\n       </a>\n       to powered cargo devices, including the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GLACIER_freezer_module" title="GLACIER freezer module">\n        GLACIER\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MERLIN_freezer_module" title="MERLIN freezer module">\n        MERLIN\n       </a>\n       freezer modules for\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_transport" title="Space transport">\n        transporting\n       </a>\n       critical science payloads.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tss20140321a_100-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tss20140321a-100">\n         [100]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="DragonLab">\n        DragonLab\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=SpaceX_Dragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: DragonLab">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       When used for non-NASA, non-ISS commercial flights, the uncrewed version of the Dragon spacecraft is called DragonLab.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-overview_88-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-overview-88">\n         [88]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It is reusable and free-flying and can carry pressurized and unpressurized payloads. Its subsystems include propulsion, power,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_Control_and_Life_Support_System" title="Environmental Control and Life Support System">\n        thermal and environmental control\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Avionics" title="Avionics">\n        avionics\n       </a>\n       , communications,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thermal_protection" title="Thermal protection">\n        thermal protection\n       </a>\n       , flight software,\n       <a href="/wiki/Guidance,_navigation,_and_control" title="Guidance, navigation, and control">\n        guidance and navigation systems\n       </a>\n       , and entry, descent, landing, and recovery gear.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sx20090918_5-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sx20090918-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It has a total combined\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Upmass" title="Upmass">\n        upmass\n       </a>\n       of 6,000 kilograms (13,000\xc2\xa0lb) upon launch, and a maximum\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Downmass" title="Downmass">\n        downmass\n       </a>\n       of 3,000 kilograms (6,600\xc2\xa0lb) when returning to Earth.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sx20090918_5-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sx20090918-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In November 2014 there were two DragonLab missions listed on the SpaceX launch manifest: one in 2016 and another in 2018.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sxManifest20141120_101-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sxManifest20141120-101">\n         [101]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, these missions were removed from the manifest in early 2017, with no official SpaceX statement.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sxManifest20141211_102-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sxManifest20141211-102">\n         [102]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The American\n       <a href="/wiki/Biosatellite_program" title="Biosatellite program">\n        Biosatellites\n       </a>\n       once performed similar uncrewed payload-delivery functions, and the Russian\n       <a href="/wiki/Bion_(satellite)" title="Bion (satellite)">\n        Bion satellites\n       </a>\n       still continue to do so.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Dragon_2">\n        Dragon 2\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=SpaceX_Dragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Dragon 2">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Dragon_2" title="Dragon 2">\n        Dragon 2\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A successor of Dragon called\n       <a href="/wiki/Dragon_2" title="Dragon 2">\n        Dragon 2\n       </a>\n       is under development by SpaceX, designed to support crewed missions. It will be able to carry up to seven astronauts, or some mix of crew and cargo, to and from\n       <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">\n        low Earth orbit\n       </a>\n       . The Dragon 2\n       <a href="/wiki/Heat_shield" title="Heat shield">\n        heat shield\n       </a>\n       is designed to withstand Earth re-entry velocities from\n       <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">\n        Lunar\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">\n        Martian\n       </a>\n       spaceflights.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2ndF9arrives_89-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2ndF9arrives-89">\n         [89]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       SpaceX has received several\n       <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">\n        U.S. Government\n       </a>\n       contracts to develop the Dragon 2 crewed variant, including a\n       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Crew_Development#CCDev_2" title="Commercial Crew Development">\n        Commercial Crew Development 2\n       </a>\n       (CCDev 2)-funded\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Act_Agreement" title="Space Act Agreement">\n        Space Act Agreement\n       </a>\n       in April 2011, and a\n       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Crew_Development#Commercial_Crew_integrated_Capability" title="Commercial Crew Development">\n        Commercial Crew integrated Capability\n       </a>\n       (CCiCap)-funded space act agreement in August 2012.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <span id="Red_Dragon">\n       </span>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Red_Dragon">\n        Red Dragon\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=SpaceX_Dragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Red Dragon">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Dragon_(spacecraft)" title="Red Dragon (spacecraft)">\n        Red Dragon (spacecraft)\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In addition to SpaceX\'s privately funded plans for an eventual\n       <a href="/wiki/Exploration_of_Mars" title="Exploration of Mars">\n        Mars mission\n       </a>\n       , NASA\n       <a href="/wiki/Ames_Research_Center" title="Ames Research Center">\n        Ames Research Center\n       </a>\n       had developed a concept called\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Dragon_(spacecraft)" title="Red Dragon (spacecraft)">\n        Red Dragon\n       </a>\n       : a low-cost Mars mission that would use\n       <a href="/wiki/Falcon_Heavy" title="Falcon Heavy">\n        Falcon Heavy\n       </a>\n       as the launch vehicle and trans-Martian injection vehicle, and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Dragon_2" title="Dragon 2">\n        Dragon 2\n       </a>\n       -based capsule to enter the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere_of_Mars" title="Atmosphere of Mars">\n        atmosphere of Mars\n       </a>\n       . The concept was originally envisioned for launch in 2018 as a\n       <a href="/wiki/Discovery_Program" title="Discovery Program">\n        NASA Discovery mission\n       </a>\n       , then alternatively for 2022, but as of September 2015\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=SpaceX_Dragon&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       it has not been yet formally submitted for funding within NASA.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wall2015_103-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Wall2015-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The objectives of the mission would be return the samples from Mars to Earth at a fraction of the cost of the NASA own return-sample mission now projected at 6 billion dollars.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wall2015_103-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Wall2015-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On 27 April 2016, SpaceX announced its plan to go ahead and launch a modified Dragon lander to Mars in 2018.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spacex-tweet-20160427_104-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-spacex-tweet-20160427-104">\n         [104]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newmann2016_105-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Newmann2016-105">\n         [105]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A Dragon capsule would perform all entry, descent and landing (EDL) functions needed to deliver payloads of 1 tonne (2,200\xc2\xa0lb) or more to the Martian surface without using a parachute. Preliminary analysis showed that the capsule\'s atmospheric drag would slow it enough for the final stage of its descent to be within the abilities of its\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SuperDraco_(rocket_engine)" title="SuperDraco (rocket engine)">\n        SuperDraco\n       </a>\n       retro-propulsion thrusters.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sdc20110731_106-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sdc20110731-106">\n         [106]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAC_2011_107-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NAC_2011-107">\n         [107]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On July 19th, 2017, however, Elon Musk announced that SpaceX had abandoned plans to continue the Red Dragon program.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">\n        <a href="#cite_note-108">\n         [108]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_Dragon_missions">\n        List of Dragon missions\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=SpaceX_Dragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: List of Dragon missions">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        List includes only completed or currently manifested missions. Launch dates are listed in\n        <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">\n         UTC\n        </a>\n        .\n       </i>\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable collapsible collapsed">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         Mission name\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Launch date (UTC)\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Remarks\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Time at ISS\n         <br/>\n         (dd hh mm)\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Outcome\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_COTS_Demo_Flight_1" title="SpaceX COTS Demo Flight 1">\n          SpX-C1\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         8 December 2010\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">\n          <a href="#cite_note-109">\n           [109]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         First Dragon mission, second Falcon 9 launch\n        </td>\n        <td class="table-na" data-sort-value="" style="background: #ececec; Thruster function was later restored and orbit corrections were made,\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frightening2013_112-1">\n          <a href="#cite_note-Frightening2013-112">\n           [112]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         but the spacecraft\'s rendezvous with the ISS was delayed from its planned date of 2 March until 3 March, when it was successfully berthed with the\n         <a href="/wiki/Harmony_(ISS_module)" title="Harmony (ISS module)">\n          <i>\n           Harmony\n          </i>\n          module\n         </a>\n         .\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">\n          <a href="#cite_note-114">\n           [114]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">\n          <a href="#cite_note-115">\n           [115]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         Dragon splashed down safely in the Pacific Ocean on 26 March.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">\n          <a href="#cite_note-116">\n           [116]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         22d 18h 14m\n        </td>\n        <td class="table-success" style="background: #bbffbb; color: black; vertical-align: middle; text-align: center;">\n         Success; spacecraft anomaly\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frightening2013_112-2">\n          <a href="#cite_note-Frightening2013-112">\n           [112]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-3" title="SpaceX CRS-3">\n          SpaceX CRS-3\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         18 April 2014\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">\n          <a href="#cite_note-117">\n           [117]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">\n          <a href="#cite_note-118">\n           [118]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         First launch of the redesigned Dragon: same\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Outer_mold_line" title="Outer mold line">\n          outer mold line\n         </a>\n         with the avionics and cargo racks redesigned to supply substantially more\n         <a href="/wiki/Solar_panels_on_spacecraft" title="Solar panels on spacecraft">\n          electric power\n         </a>\n         to powered cargo devices, including additional cargo freezers (\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GLACIER_freezer_module" title="GLACIER freezer module">\n          GLACIER\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MERLIN_freezer_module" title="MERLIN freezer module">\n          MERLIN\n         </a>\n         ) for transporting critical science payloads.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tss20140321a_100-1">\n          <a href="#cite_note-tss20140321a-100">\n           [100]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         Launch rescheduled for 18 April due to a helium leak.\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         27d 21h 49m\n        </td>\n        <td class="table-success" style="background: #bbffbb; color: black; vertical-align: middle; text-align: center;">\n         Success\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Launch_119-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-Launch-119">\n           [119]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-4" title="SpaceX CRS-4">\n          SpaceX CRS-4\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <span class="nowrap">\n          21 September 2014\n         </span>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SpaceflightNowTrackingStation_120-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-SpaceflightNowTrackingStation-120">\n           [120]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         First launch of a Dragon with living payload, in the form of 20 mice which are part of a NASA experiment to study the physiological effects of long-duration spaceflight.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">\n          <a href="#cite_note-121">\n           [121]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         31d 22h 41m\n        </td>\n        <td class="table-success" style="background: #bbffbb; color: black; vertical-align: middle; text-align: center;">\n         Success\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">\n          <a href="#cite_note-122">\n           [122]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-5" title="SpaceX CRS-5">\n          SpaceX CRS-5\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         10 January 2015\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SpaceflightNowTrackingStation_120-1">\n          <a href="#cite_note-SpaceflightNowTrackingStation-120">\n           [120]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Cargo manifest change due to\n         <a href="/wiki/Cygnus_CRS_Orb-3" title="Cygnus CRS Orb-3">\n          Cygnus CRS Orb-3\n         </a>\n         launch failure.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">\n          <a href="#cite_note-123">\n           [123]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         Carried the\n         <a href="/wiki/Cloud_Aerosol_Transport_System" title="Cloud Aerosol Transport System">\n          Cloud Aerosol Transport System\n         </a>\n         experiment.\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         29d 03h 17m\n        </td>\n        <td class="table-success" style="background: #bbffbb;       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=SpaceX_Dragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Specifications">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Size_comparison_of_Apollo,_Orion_and_Dragon_spacecraft.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="2400" height="73" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Size_comparison_of_Apollo%2C_Orion_and_Dragon_spacecraft.svg/220px-Size_comparison_of_Apollo%2C_Orion_and_Dragon_spacecraft.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Size_comparison_of_Apollo%2C_Orion_and_Dragon_spacecraft.svg/330px-Size_comparison_of_Apollo%2C_Orion_and_Dragon_spacecraft.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Size_comparison_of_Apollo%2C_Orion_and_Dragon_spacecraft.svg/440px-Size_comparison_of_Apollo%2C_Orion_and_Dragon_spacecraft.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Size_comparison_of_Apollo,_Orion_and_Dragon_spacecraft.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Size comparison of the\n         <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Command/Service_Module" title="Apollo Command/Service Module">\n          Apollo\n         </a>\n         (left),\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orion_capsule" title="Orion capsule">\n          Orion\n         </a>\n         (center) and Dragon (right) capsules\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="DragonLab_2">\n        DragonLab\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=SpaceX_Dragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: DragonLab">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The following specifications are published by SpaceX for the non-NASA, non-ISS commercial flights of the refurbished Dragon capsules, listed as "DragonLab" flights on the SpaceX manifest. The specifications for the NASA-contracted Dragon Cargo were not included in the 2009 DragonLab datasheet.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sx20090918_5-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sx20090918-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dt>\n        Pressure vessel\n       </dt>\n      </dl>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        10\xc2\xa0m\n        <sup>\n         3\n        </sup>\n        (350\xc2\xa0cu\xc2\xa0ft) interior pressurized, environmentally controlled, payload volume.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sx20090918_5-7">\n         <a href="#cite_note-sx20090918-5">\n          [5]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Onboard environment: 10\xe2\x80\x9346\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (50\xe2\x80\x93115\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F);\n        <a href="/wiki/Relative_humidity" title="Relative humidity">\n         relative humidity\n        </a>\n        25~75%; 13.9~14.9\n        <a href="/wiki/Pounds_per_square_inch#Psig_v._Psia" title="Pounds per square inch">\n         psia\n        </a>\n        air pressure (958.4~1027\n        <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">\n         hPa\n        </a>\n        ).\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sx20090918_5-8">\n         <a href="#cite_note-sx20090918-5">\n          [5]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <dl>\n       <dt>\n        Unpressurized sensor bay (recoverable payload)\n       </dt>\n      </dl>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        0.1\xc2\xa0m\n        <sup>\n         3\n        </sup>\n        (3.5\xc2\xa0cu\xc2\xa0ft) unpressurized payload volume.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Sensor bay hatch opens after orbit insertion to allow full sensor access to the\n        <a href="/wiki/Outer_space" title="Outer space">\n         outer space\n        </a>\n        environment, and closes before Earth atmosphere re-entry.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sx20090918_5-9">\n         <a href="#cite_note-sx20090918-5">\n          [5]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <dl>\n       <dt>\n        Unpressurized trunk (non-recoverable)\n       </dt>\n      </dl>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        14\xc2\xa0m\n        <sup>\n         3\n        </sup>\n        (490\xc2\xa0cu\xc2\xa0ft) payload volume in the 2.3\xc2\xa0m (7\xc2\xa0ft 7\xc2\xa0in) trunk, aft of the pressure vessel heat shield, with optional trunk extension to 4.3\xc2\xa0m (14\xc2\xa0ft 1\xc2\xa0in) total length, payload volume increases to 34\xc2\xa0m\n        <sup>\n         3\n        </sup>\n        (1,200\xc2\xa0cu\xc2\xa0ft).\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sx20090918_5-10">\n         <a href="#cite_note-sx20090918-5">\n          [5]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Supports sensors and space apertures up to 3.5\xc2\xa0m (11\xc2\xa0ft 6\xc2\xa0in) in diameter.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sx20090918_5-11">\n         <a href="#cite_note-sx20090918-5">\n          [5]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <dl>\n       <dt>\n        Power,\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spacecraft_communication" title="Spacecraft communication">\n         communication\n        </a>\n        and command systems\n       </dt>\n      </dl>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        Power: twin\n        <a href="/wiki/Solar_panel" title="Solar panel">\n         solar panels\n        </a>\n        providing 1,500\xc2\xa0W average, 4,000\xc2\xa0W peak, at 28 and 120\n        <a href="/wiki/Volt" title="Volt">\n         V\n         <sub>\n          DC\n         </sub>\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sx20090918_5-12">\n         <a href="#cite_note-sx20090918-5">\n          [5]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Spacecraft communications: commercial standard\n        <a href="/wiki/RS-422" title="RS-422">\n         RS-422\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/MIL-STD-1553" title="MIL-STD-1553">\n         military standard 1553\n        </a>\n        serial I/O, plus\n        <a href="/wiki/Ethernet" title="Ethernet">\n         Ethernet\n        </a>\n        communications for\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internet_protocol" title="Internet protocol">\n         IP\n        </a>\n        -addressable standard payload service.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Command\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uplink" title="Uplink">\n         uplink\n        </a>\n        : 300\xc2\xa0k\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bits_per_second" title="Bits per second">\n         bps\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sx20090918_5-13">\n         <a href="#cite_note-sx20090918-5">\n          [5]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Telemetry" title="Telemetry">\n         Telemetry\n        </a>\n        /data\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Downlink" title="Downlink">\n         downlink\n        </a>\n        : 300\xc2\xa0Mbit/s standard,\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fault-tolerant_system" title="Fault-tolerant system">\n         fault-tolerant\n        </a>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S-band" title="S-band">\n         S-band\n        </a>\n        telemetry and video transmitters.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sx20090918_5-14">\n         <a href="#cite_note-sx20090918-5">\n          [5]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Radiation_tolerance">\n        Radiation tolerance\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=SpaceX_Dragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Radiation tolerance">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Dragon uses a "radiation-tolerant" design in the electronic hardware and software that make up its\n       <a href="/wiki/Category:Avionics_computers" title="Category:Avionics computers">\n        flight computers\n       </a>\n       . The system uses three pairs of computers, each constantly checking on the others, to instantiate a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fault-tolerant_design" title="Fault-tolerant design">\n        fault-tolerant design\n       </a>\n       . In the event of a radiation upset or soft error, one of the computer pairs will perform a\n       <a href="/wiki/Reboot_(computing)" title="Reboot (computing)">\n        soft reboot\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aw20121118_33-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-aw20121118-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Including the six computers that make up the main flight computers, Dragon employs a total of 18 triple-processor computers.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aw20121118_33-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-aw20121118-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=SpaceX_Dragon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: See also">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation"
